ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-item {
    counter-increment: list-counter-alpha;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-alpha, lower-alpha);
}

/* Level 3: Lowercase roman numerals */

    counter-reset: list-counter-roman;
}

    counter-increment: list-counter-roman;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-roman, lower-roman);
}

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="module-competence">Module Competence<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-competence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This module is designed to enable the learner apply the concepts and principles of Microbiology and Parasitology in prevention and control of diseases.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="module-units">Module Units<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-units" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="module-outcomes">Module Outcomes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-outcomes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Demonstrate understanding of the concepts of Parasitology in prevention of diseases</li>
<li>Demonstrate understanding of the concepts of microbiology in prevention of diseases</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="module-content">Module content<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Parasitology</strong>: Definitions, classification of parasites, modes of transmission, lifecycle, clinical importance, treatment, prevention and control of Helminths (Cestodes- Taenia saginata, Taenia solium and Echinococcus granulosas, Trematodes- flukes, Nematodes- roundworms), Protozoa (Entamoeba, Giardia, Leishmania, Balantidium, Plasmodium. Arthropods.</p>
<p><strong>Microbiology</strong>: Classification of microorganisms and clinical importance, Concept of infection, Normal flora, Bacterial pathogens: Staphyloccocus aureus, Streptococcus pyogenes, Streptococcus agalactiae, Streptococcus pneumonia, Viridans streptococci, Enterococcus species, Bacillus anthracis, Corynebacterium diphtheria, Listeria monocytogenes, Clostridium perfringens, Clostridium botulism, Clostridium tetani, Neisseria meningitides, Neisseria gonorrhea, Escherichia coli, Shigellaammonellae, Klebsiellae, Proteus mirabilis, Vibrio cholera, Pseudomonas, Brucella species, Haemophilus influenza, Mycobacterium tuberculosis, Treponema pallidum.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition-of-terms-in-parasitology">DEFINITION OF TERMS IN PARASITOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-terms-in-parasitology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Parasitology- Science that deals with organisms that live temporarily or permanently on/within other living organisms for the purpose of procuring food and the relationship of this organisms to their hosts</li>
<li>Endo parasite- live inside body e.g. Tenia saginata</li>
<li>Permanent Parasite- spends major part</li>
<li>Temporary parasite- only make contact to the host e.g. bed bugs</li>
<li>Facultative parasites- Live either paristic or free lives e.g. hookworms</li>
<li>Obligate- In capable of living independently.</li>
<li>Auto Heteroxenous parasites- A definitive host of one generation becomes the intermediate host of another generation.</li>
<li>Pathogenic Parasites- Parasite that causes injury to host e.g. mechanical, traumatic or toxic</li>
<li>Parasite- Organism which lives in another organism and derives its food from another host and gives nothing in turn.</li>
<li>Definitive Host  Host in which parasite reaches maturity e.g. man in case of taenia saginata</li>
<li>Intermediate host- Host where parasite undergoes preliminary development .g taenia saginata in bovine</li>
<li>Reservoir- Source of Infestation</li>
<li>Cyst- Larvae stage of parasite, no development goes on in this stage.</li>
<li>Encystment- Process of forming a cyst</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="host-parasite-association">HOST-PARASITE ASSOCIATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#host-parasite-association" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Parasites and hosts interact in the following ways;</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Parasitism</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An association where one organism is harmed while the other benefits. E.g. Ascaris lumbricoides residing in the intestinal tract of man to feed on the food in the intestines resulting to infections</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Mutualism</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An association where both parasite and host benefits from the relationship</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Whereby organisms benefit each other but one can live an independent life (independency)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Commensalism</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An association where a parasite benefits from the relationship without causing any harm to the host</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Whereby an organism lives in the host, confers no benefit nor harm except where the hosts immunity impairs then the it can become an opportunist</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An association between two organisms in which one benefits and the other derives neither benefit nor harm.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Symbiosis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>relationship where the parasite and the host benefit each other and cannot live independent of each other (dependency)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Requirements of Parasites</p>
<ul>
<li>
<ol>
<li>Nutrients</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="2">
<li>Warmth</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="3">
<li>Comfort</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="4">
<li>Protection</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="5">
<li>Moisture</li>
</ol>
</li>
</ul>

<p>PARASITES OF PUBLIC HEALTH IMPORTANCE</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The classification of parasites is controversial as there is no universally accepted system.</li>
<li>The most acceptable taxonomic classification of human parasites includes:</li>
<li>Endoparasites and Ectoparasites.</li>
<li>Endoparasites are sub-classified into Helminthic parasites and Protozoan parasites.</li>
</ul>
<p>Helminthic parasites are either flat worms (Trematodes), segmented ribbon like worms (Cestodes) or cylindrical worms (Nematodes).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-of-parasites">Classification of parasites<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-parasites" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Parasites occur in two distinct forms:-</p>
<p> Single-celled protozoa
 Multicellular metozoa helminths</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="protozoa">PROTOZOA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protozoa" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>They are unicellular (single-celled)</p>
<p>They have a specific shape</p>
<p>They consist of a true membrane bound nucleus and cytoplasm</p>
<ul>
<li>They are divided into four (4) groups;
 Amoeba; move by pseudopodia
 Flagellates; move by flagella
 Ciliates; move by cilia
 Sporozoa; exhibits a slight amoebic movement</li>
</ul>
<p>Examples</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Amoeba; Entamoeba histolytica</p>
<p>Flagellates; Giardia lamblia</p>
<p>Ciliates; Balantidim coli</p>
<p>Sporozoa; Plasmodium species (vivax, malariae, ovale, falciparum)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-57c22d15.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg">
E. histolytica cyst
E. histolytica trophozoite
A Protozoan parasite, Entamoeba histolytica (cyst &amp; trophozoite)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="helminths-worms">HELMINTHS (WORMS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#helminths-worms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>&gt; Helminths cause much disease and are the largest of human parasites, also known as soil transmitted worms.</p>
<ul>
<li>Helminths of medical importance are divided into three zoological classes, namely</li>
<li>Cestodes(tapeworms)</li>
<li>Nematodes(round worms)</li>
<li>Trematodes(flukes)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="morphology-of-the-helminths">MORPHOLOGY OF THE HELMINTHS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#morphology-of-the-helminths" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cestodes">CESTODES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cestodes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li> They have a segmented tape-like shape</li>
<li> Head end has suckers with hooks</li>
<li> Have no alimentary canal</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nematodes">NEMATODES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nematodes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>They have an elongated cylindrical shape</li>
<li>Head end have no suckers and hooks(lack)</li>
<li>Have a complete alimentary canal(present and complete)</li>
<li>Have a body cavity</li>
<li>The sexes are separated(diecious)</li>
<li>Examples include; Ascaris lumbricoides (roundworms)
Enterobius vermicularis (pin worm)
Trichuris trichuria ((whip worm)
Ancylostoma duodenale (hook worm)</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-4c5c2705.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<p>A Nematode worm, Ascaris lumbricoides</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="trematodes">TREMATODES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#trematodes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p> They have a leaf-like unsegmented body
 Head end have suckers with no hooks
 Alimentary canal is present but incomplete
 Have no body cavity
 The sexes are not separated (monoecious) except flukes which is (diecious)
 Examples are; flat like worms commonly found in lungs, liver, brain and tissues.</p>
<p>They include; Schistosoma species (haematobium, japonicum, mansoni, interlactum)
Fasciola hepatica (accidental for human beings)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-e452820d.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors-factors-influencing-parasitic-infections">PREDISPOSING FACTORS/FACTORS INFLUENCING PARASITIC INFECTIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors-factors-influencing-parasitic-infections" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-poor-disposal-of-wastes">1. Poor disposal of wastes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-poor-disposal-of-wastes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>These include poor sanitation and improper disposal of wastes including fecal matter.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
5 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Conducive environment (has predisposing conditions) that favor the agents such that when introduced can be transmitted to other organisms.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-nutrition">2. Nutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Availability of the nutrients for the parasites enables them to lodge, establish and multiply</li>
<li>If the host has sufficient or abundant nutrients, the adverse effects of the parasites may not be amplified or noticed.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-age">3. Age<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-age" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Mostly the young toddlers/children are explorative and will put anything in their mouth that they come across hence infestation of the worms if the substance is contaminated</li>
<li>Also vulnerable groups such as the under-five, gravida and the old, their immunological status is low leading to rise in infestations or prone to infestations.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-nature-of-occupation">4. Nature of occupation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-nature-of-occupation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Activities that one does for a living may expose him/her to infestations. E.g. fishing or farming in Schistosoma cercaries infested waters</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-individual-lifestyle">5. Individual lifestyle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-individual-lifestyle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Includes the habits and practices i.e. pastoralists communities are likely to consume partially cooked or raw meat/beef hence high chances of infestation.</li>
<li>Also affluent societies eat raw vegetables e.g. carrots and lettuce which may be contaminated with the worms.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-rearing-of-domestic-animals">6. Rearing of domestic animals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-rearing-of-domestic-animals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>E.g. cattle, sheep, goats, dogs etc. can expose one to worms like the Taenia saginata (cow tapeworm) so having cattle can put one at risk of the infestation with these worms</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-incorrect-improper-meat-inspection">7. Incorrect/improper meat inspection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-incorrect-improper-meat-inspection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>This could result in infestations to people eating meat</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effects-of-parasites-to-the-host">EFFECTS OF PARASITES TO THE HOST<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-parasites-to-the-host" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cause trauma by damaging tissues and organs where they are lodged</li>
<li>Causes anemia- they deplete blood causing normocytic anemia</li>
<li>Compete with the host for food nutrients resulting to malnutrition of the affected host</li>
<li>Some causes indigestion e.g. Taenia saginata they cause indigestion in the cow</li>
<li>They cause blockage of vessels and organs e.g. fish tapeworm in the fish intestines</li>
<li>Immunosuppression- bilharzia, malaria etc. leads to certain degree of immune suppression which renders the infected host to other diseases</li>
<li>Anaphylactic shock- maybe induced by sudden release of larger amounts of parasites into the blood stream</li>
<li>Allergic reactions- in the case of River blindness, the presence of filarial worms under the skin leads to depigmentation due to allergic reactions</li>
<li>Mechanical damage- in the cases of Ascaris infections, the presence of the worms in the intestines may lead to intestinal damage</li>
<li>Physical damage- caused by irritation of the skin and tissues by the ecto and endoparasites</li>
<li>Cause/source of nuisance- e.g. mosquito noise disrupt the sleeping patterns of the people</li>
<li>Super infections- in the case of (muco) cutaneous leishmaniasis, ulceration may lead to super infections with the bacteria</li>
<li>Production of toxic compounds- it's thought that African trypanosome when it's in the central nervous system, it produces aromatic amino acid analogues which influence the brain functioning</li>
<li>Reduces the host population size through death</li>
<li>Cause tumors for the case of Cysticercus bovis in the cow</li>
<li>Leads to severe loss of weight in both animals and man (hosts)</li>
<li>Can cause medical complications e.g. fits (when the ova of Echinococcus granulosus is lodged in the dog brain)</li>
<li>Cause psychological discomforts e.g. crawling of the tapeworms</li>
<li>Reduces productivity of the host</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>PREVENTION AND CONTROL MEASURES OF PARASITES</p>
<ul>
<li>Use of chemicals for spraying especially the ectoparasites</li>
<li>Proper cooking of beef and other vegetables</li>
<li>Proper washing of fruits and vegetables before consumption</li>
<li>Regular deworming of animals and man</li>
<li>Proper waste management (excreta and other wastes)</li>
<li>Treating or boiling water before drinking</li>
<li>Proper meat inspection</li>
<li>Proper hygiene</li>
<li>Wearing of shoes /gumboots while walking in water or swampy water infested with worms</li>
<li>Chemotherapy-preventive chemotherapy for school-going children such as deworming</li>
<li>Health education and promotion on proper hygiene</li>
<li>Improve access to clean water and sanitation</li>
<li>Avoid swimming/bathing in water infested with worms</li>
<li>Drainage of stagnant water to prevent breeding of mosquito larvae</li>
<li>Use of bed nets to prevent mosquito bites</li>
<li>Washing hands regularly especially after handling raw food and fecal matter</li>
<li>Periodic examination of food handlers to prevent cross-contamination of food</li>
<li>Get rid of intermediate host</li>
<li>Zero grazing/rotational grazing</li>
<li>Proper storage of food to avoid mechanical damage</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="parasites-life-cycle">Parasites' Life Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#parasites-life-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Life cycles of parasites may be simple or complex. Parasites that are characterized by a simple or direct life cycle have only one host and are described as <strong>monoxenous</strong> (e.g. life cycle of <em>Ascaris lumbricoides</em>).</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The parasite generally spends most of its life in or on the host, and may reproduce within the host. Because offspring must be transmitted to other hosts, however, the parasite or its progeny must have some way of leaving the host, surviving in the external environment for some period, and locating and infecting a new host.</p>
<p>Parasites with simple life cycles have both parasitic and free living life stages. The proportion of the total life cycle spent in each stage varies according to the parasite.</p>
<ul>
<li>Parasites with more complex life cycles involving multiple hosts are described as having indirect or heteroxenous life cycles (e.g. life cycle of Fasciola spp).</li>
<li>The primary or definitive host of a heteroxenous species is the one in which adult parasites live and reproduce sexually.</li>
<li>The secondary or intermediate host (IH) is the host where immature life stages of the parasite live and reproduce asexually.</li>
</ul>
<p>In many cases, the parasite passes through critical developmental stages in the IH. The latter may also aid in transmitting parasites to their final host. Rat flea, for example, is the IH for mammalian parasites such as the tapeworm; Hymenolepis diminuta.</p>
<ul>
<li>Some parasites are transmitted directly from one host to another, often by insects, described as vectors.</li>
</ul>
<p>One particularly effective vector for vertebrate parasites is the mosquito, which plays a role in transmission of numerous parasites including heartworm, the viruses that cause yellow fever and encephalitis, and Plasmodium, the protozoan that causes malaria.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tape-worms">Tape worms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tape-worms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>They are mainly three types:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Taenia Sagnata</li>
<li>Taenia solium</li>
<li>Dyphyllobothrium latum - fish tapeworm</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>a) Taenia Sagnata</p>
<ul>
<li>Disease caused is taeniasis</li>
<li>Distributed in tropical Africa, Europe and parts of Asia</li>
</ul>
<p>Life Cycle</p>
<p> Adults are found in the small intestines of man; mating takes place, eggs are laid and gravid proglotids (Ripe eggs come out together with feaces), animals (cattle) ingest the eggs and egg travel via digestive system to reach stomach and then to intestines (onchosphere) penetrates walls of small intestines to reach lymphatic system, travel via lymphatic system to reach their places of predilection (active muscles; heart, tongue, massetta muscles, diaphragm). Here they become quiescent (inactive/dormant) and encyst forming cystcercus bovis. If animal is slaughtered man ingests infested beef and the cycle continues.</p>
<p>Symptom/ pathology</p>
<ol>
<li>Anemia in infested person</li>
<li>Fever</li>
<li>General malaise</li>
<li>Headaches</li>
<li>Blood spots in stool</li>
</ol>
<p>Prevention/control</p>
<ol>
<li>Treat the sick</li>
<li>Create awareness on methods of prevention and control</li>
<li>Carry out lab examination on suspects for proper treatment</li>
<li>Safe disposal of feaces</li>
<li>Treat herbivorous animals</li>
<li>Thorough meat inspection and judgment</li>
<li>Fencing grazing areas</li>
</ol>
<p>b) Dyphylobothrium latum</p>
<p>Distribution- cosmopolitan</p>
<p>Disease caused is Dyphyllobothriasis</p>
<p>Location- small intestines</p>
<p><strong>Life Cycle</strong></p>
<p> Adult are found in small intestines of man. Male and females are found in the intestines together. Mating takes place, eggs are laid and come together with feaces. These eggs develop into an ovum which develop into an ovum which develop into caracidium (ciliated larvae). The caracidium escapes into water and swims. It is ingested by cylops (water fleas, planktons). It travels into the cards of the cyclops and develop into procercoid. Fish ingests infested cyclop. The procercoid penetrate the muscles of fish and develop into procercoid. Here the larvae are encysted and remain infective throughout the life of fish. If man ingest infested fish either raw or uncooked the larvae emerge and go via digestive system to reach small intestines where they develop into adults.</p>
<p><strong>Clinical manifestation/ symptoms</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Abdominal pain.</li>
<li>Vomiting</li>
<li>Anaemia</li>
<li>Multiple infestation; cause obstruction in the intestines</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Prevention/Control</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Treatment of the sick.</li>
<li>Create awareness</li>
<li>Safe disposal of feaces</li>
<li>Inspection of the fish and make a good judgment.</li>
<li>Safe water without cyclops</li>
<li>Refrigeration of fish at 10 C for 15 minutes</li>
<li>Prevent discharge of raw sewage into water bodies.</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>Proper cooking of fish</li>
</ol>
<p>c) Taenia Solium</p>
<p>Distribution- cosmopolitan</p>
<p>Disease- Taeniasis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="life-cycle">Life Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#life-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p> Adults are found in the small intestines of man. Mating takes place, eggs are laid and come out with together with feaces. The eggs rapture after leaving man and hatch into larvae (onchosphere) if pig ingest the onchosphere, they travel via the digestive system and enter the circulatory system and commonly the lymphatic system where they are taken to places of predilection(skeletal muscles, visceral organs, heart, diaphragm, tongue and on abdominal muscles). If man ingests infested pork, the cycle continues.</p>
<p> Animals commonly affected</p>
<p>Man, dog- definitive host</p>
<p>Deer, sheep, cattle- intermediate host</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-and-control">Prevention and Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-and-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Treat the sick</li>
<li>Create awareness</li>
<li>Thorough inspection of pork.</li>
<li>Safe disposal of feaces.</li>
<li>Thorough cooking.</li>
<li>Restrict pigs</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="trichinella-spiralis">Trichinella Spiralis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#trichinella-spiralis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Disease- Trichinosis</p>
<p>Distribution: worldwide except Asia and Australia</p>
<p>It has definitive host and intermediate host together e.g. man, cats, dogs, pigs, rats and carnivorous animals.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p> How man is infected- ingestion of raw pork. Larvae pass through digestive system to reach intestines and develop into adults. Females barrow walls of the intestines and lay eggs. Eggs hatch into larvae. Larvae enter the circulatory system and are transported to places of predilection (tongue, diaphragm, striated muscle) where they encyst and form coil. If man ingests infested pork, larvae emerge.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-control">Prevention/Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Treat the sick</li>
<li>Create awareness</li>
<li>Thorough meat inspection and judgment</li>
<li>Thorough cooking of pork.</li>
<li>Restrict pigs</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="on-examination">On Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#on-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="trichuris-trichiura-whip-worm-disease">Trichuris Trichiura (whip worm disease)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#trichuris-trichiura-whip-worm-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Causes: Trichiuriasis</li>
<li>Distribution- cosmopolitan but common in East Africa.</li>
<li>Definitive host- man</li>
<li>Intermediate host- Nil</li>
<li>How man is infected- Ingestion of un-hatched larvae</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="life-cycle-of-trichuris-trichiura-whip-worm">Life Cycle of Trichuris Trichiura (whip worm)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#life-cycle-of-trichuris-trichiura-whip-worm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="life-cycle">Life Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#life-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p> Adults are found in the small intestines of man. Mating takes place here. Gravid females lay eggs about 2000 per day. Adult bury the head in the wall of small intestines in a whip like form. Eggs come out together with feaces. Man swallows eggs or un hatched larvae. They pass through the mouth, oesophagus to stomach where eggs are dissolved larvae emerge and go to small intestines where they mature to adults. The cycle continues.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-in-man">Effects in Man<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-in-man" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p> During the process of burying whip like head in the mucous membrane of small intestine there is no apparent damage.
 Areas of local inflammation
 Depending on the dose/number they may cause Appendicitis</p>
<p>Diagnosis- Ova in feaces</p>
<p>Treatment- use antihelminths</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-control">Prevention/Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Safe disposal of feaces</li>
<li>Personal hygiene</li>
<li>Boiling water</li>
<li>Wash vegetables</li>
<li>Treatment of all the sick people</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="strogyloides-stercolaris">Strogyloides stercolaris<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#strogyloides-stercolaris" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p> Facultative parasite
 Causes strogyloidosis
 Distribution- cosmopolitan
 Definitive host- man
 Intermediate host- nill
 How man is infected; penetration of skin by filarial larvae</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="life-cycle-strogyloides-stercolaris">Life Cycle - Strogyloides stercolaris<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#life-cycle-strogyloides-stercolaris" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Fillarial form larvae penetrates skin of man. It enters blood circulatory system to reach lungs. In lungs they ascend through trachea where they are swallowed. They go to stomach- intestines and develop into adults. Eggs are laid and come out with feaces. The eggs hatch into filarial form larvae. (Rhabidth form larvae)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="symptoms">Symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Irritation at the point of penetration</li>
<li>During migration; ill feeling, fever, urticaria (change of color at the point of penetration), difficult breathing, mild broncho pneumonia</li>
<li>When they develop into adults; diarrhoea</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Ova in feaces/ Rabiditi form</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effects-in-man">Effects in Man<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-in-man" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<ol>
<li>Raised blotches (red)</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="2">
<li>Inflammation of the respiratory system</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="3">
<li>Pneumonia</li>
</ol>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-control">Prevention/ control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Safe disposal of feaces</li>
<li>Protect the skin (wearing shoes)</li>
<li>Carry out treatment of the sick</li>
<li>Create awareness on methods of prevention and control</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ankylostomes-hook-worm">Ankylostomes (Hook worm)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ankylostomes-hook-worm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p> Disease: Ankylostosomias (hook worm disease)
 Types of hookworms that commonly affect man</p>
<p>i. Ankylostoma duodenale
ii. Ankylostoma caninum</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>iii. Ankylostoma Brazilianze
iv. Ankylostoma Americanus</p>
<p> Distribution- Tropical areas, America
 Definitive host </p>
<p>} Ankylostoma Americanus</p>
<p>Ankylostoma Duodenale man</p>
<p>} Ankylostoma Caninum</p>
<p>Ankylostoma Brazilianze Cats/ dogs</p>
<p>Intermediate host: Nill</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="life-cycle-of-ankylostomes-hook-worm">Life Cycle of Ankylostomes (Hook worm)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#life-cycle-of-ankylostomes-hook-worm" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p> Fillarial form larvae penetrate through the skin of man. They travel via circulatory system to reach the heart. From heart to lungs and ascend through trachea where they are swallowed and go through digestive system then develop into adults in the small intestines. After mating the gravid (ripe) females lay eggs (between 24,000- 30,000 a day). Ripe eggs come out together with feaces and hatch into filarial form larvae. If the filarial form larvae penetrate the skin of man, cycle continues.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms">Symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Larvae migrans or creeping eruption is visible on the skin (produces intense irritation</li>
<li>Ground itch on point of entry (redness, irritation may be ulcerative. If the point attracts pus forming bacteria (likely to form abscess)</li>
<li>During migration- cough, sneezing, pneumonia, fever</li>
<li>Adult stage- cause abdominal pains, general weakness</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-in-man">Effects in man<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-in-man" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Visible damage of the subcutaneous layer of the skin</li>
<li>Supprative sores at point of entry or between toes</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Potential haemorrhages in the lungs and possible pneumonia.</li>
<li>Haemorrhages in the small intestines and mucosa</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ova in faeces</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Use anti-helminths</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-control">Prevention/Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Safe disposal of feaces</li>
<li>Protection of skin</li>
<li>Treatment of the sick</li>
<li>Create awareness</li>
<li>Personal hygiene</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="plasmodium">Plasmodium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#plasmodium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Causes - malaria</li>
<li>Distribution - cosmopolitan</li>
<li>Disease - Malaria</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="it-has-two-phases">It has two phases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#it-has-two-phases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Sexual Phase - known as sporogony take place in intestinal tract of the mosquito</li>
<li>Asexual phase - known as schizogony; occurs in human host.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="life-cycle">Life Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#life-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Sporozite - are infective form of plasmodium found in salivary glands of female anophline mosquitoes.</li>
<li>Saliva containing sporozites is infected to man through a mosquito bite. (blood stream through proboscis)</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:kenyaewakili@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">kenyaewakili@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>After circulating in blood circulation for about 20-30 minutes, they enter carenchymal cells of the liver- begin to multiply (This stage is referred to as erythrocytic stage)</li>
<li>In 10 days multiply small forms called merozoites break out of the liver cells and are released into the circulatory system and seek to enter erythrocytes</li>
<li>In the erythrocytes (intra- erythrocytic stage) a series of development takes place and form a ring form known as trophozoite and depending on space they enlarge and divide into segments known as schizonts. Individual schizonts are known as merozoites</li>
<li>When mature schizonts rapture from erythrocytes the merozoites are released into the circulation and seek to enter uninfected erythrocytes.</li>
<li>The period of release of merozoites into circulation accounts for fever (mostly in 2 days) plasmodium vivax (tartian). (3 days) plasmodium falciparum (quartan)</li>
<li>After multiple erythrocytic cycles, some merozoites transform themselves into sexual macrogametocytes (female) and others into microgametocytes (males)</li>
<li>If a mosquito bites a human being with malaria gametocytes are ingested with blood meal</li>
<li>In the mosquito stomach microgametocytes develop flagella. Microgametocytes break free and penetrate macrogametocytes and produce a zygote (fertilized)</li>
<li>Zygote enter mosquito wall, develop into ookinetes which develop into oocyst and sporozites eventually break out of body cavity and migrate to the salivary glands. When the mosquito bites uninfected man, the sporozoites are squeezed from salivary glands into circulatory system of man and the cycle continues.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-plasmodium">Types of Plasmodium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-plasmodium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<ol>
<li>Plasmodium Vivax</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="2">
<li>Plasmodium fulciparum</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="3">
<li>Plasmodium Ovale</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="4">
<li>Plasmodium Malariae</li>
</ol>
</li>
</ul>
<p>N/B- P. vivax and p. falciparum are more common causes of malaria than are p. ovale and p. malriae.</p>

<li>Physical control- clearing bushes &amp; draining of stagnant water</li>
<li>Chemicals</li>
<li>Align gutters</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="enterobius-vermicularis-oxyuris-vermicularis">Enterobius Vermicularis (oxyuris Vermicularis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#enterobius-vermicularis-oxyuris-vermicularis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Disease caused- Enterobiasis, (pin worm)</li>
<li>Distribution- cosmopolitan  worlwide</li>
<li>Definitive host- man</li>
<li>Intermediate- Nill</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="life-cycle">Life Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#life-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When eggs are swallowed they pass to the duodenum where they hatch. They move to small intestines where they mount (mating takes place) gravid females shift to the caecum. Eggs are laid and come out with feaces. They do not develop until they are swallowed by man again. The cycle continues.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms">Symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Nocturnal migration causes intense irritation in anal and genital region.</li>
<li>Sleeplessness</li>
<li>In adult- abdominal pains</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-to-man">Effects to man<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-to-man" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Scratching may bring secondary infection</li>
<li>Due to the presence of adults in the intestines, it may cause inflammation of the membrane (mucosa) and possible appendicitis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Parasites in feaces</li>
<li>Treatment- use anti-helminths (current)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-control">Prevention/control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<ol>
<li>Personal hygiene (strict) mostly washing hands</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="2">
<li>Frequent washing of beddings and clothing</li>
</ol>
</li>
</ul>

<li>Application of soothing oil to ease irritation.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ascaries-lumbricoides">Ascaries lumbricoides<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ascaries-lumbricoides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Disease- Ascariasis (roundworm infection)</li>
<li>Distribution- cosmopolitan</li>
<li>Definitive host- man, pigs</li>
<li>Intermediate host- nill</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="life-cycle">Life Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#life-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Man ingest un-hatched larvae, they go via digestive system to intestine then penetrate intestinal wall, go via the blood circulatory system up to the lungs where they moult (cast off their outer covering) and then migrate to the bronchi and ascend to the mouth. They travel through the digestive system again to the intestines where they develop into adults. Mating takes place and gravid eggs come out with feaces. The eggs develop into infective larvae with soil or water. If man ingests infective larvae the cycle continues.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms">Symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>During the larval stage- Fever (urticaria), change of skin colour, coughing</li>
<li>Adult stage- inflammation of mucus membrane of intestines, pneumonia, abdominal discomforts, loss of appetite</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis-treatment">Diagnosis &amp; Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ova in feaces</li>
<li>Use of anti-helminths</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-control">Prevention/ Control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Safe disposal of feaces</li>
<li>Personal hygiene</li>
<li>Boiling of water</li>
<li>Cook vegetables</li>
</ol>

<li>Treatment of the sick</li>
<li>Create awareness</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wucheria-barncrofti">Wucheria Barncrofti<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wucheria-barncrofti" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Causes disease  filariasis</li>
<li>Distribution- Cosmopolitan mostly in tropical countries</li>
<li>Definitive host- man</li>
<li>Intermediate host- culex fatigans, anopheles gambiae, culex paedes are capable of aiding transmission</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="life-cycle">Life Cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#life-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Larvae enters the skin through penetration by a bite by mosquito pass via circulatory system or lymphatic to reach the nodes</li>
<li>In nodes they mature and develop into microfilarial.</li>
<li>Mature microfilarial pass through walls of the lymphatic system to the blood circulatory system.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-in-man">Effects in man<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-in-man" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Acute - Lymph nodes become dropsical, enlarged due to toxic reaction, the node become necrotic (death of part of living tissue)</li>
<li>Sub acute - Thickening of node wall/ lymphagitis (inflammation of node wall)</li>
<li>Chronic- Collection of fibrous tissue in the node succeeded/ followed by calcification of worm also followed by pools of lymph within the node</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms">Symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Acute stage - Numbness, weakness, aches in limbs, head ache, loss of appetite, insomnia (sleeping)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the genitals are involved; pain and lymph nodes are enlarged</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chronic stage - Lymph nodes are enlarged, obstruction of lymphatics causing genital enlargement and elephantiasis in various parts of the body (legs, hands) etc.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>On lab examination larvae are easily seen</li>
</ul>
